# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes ConfigMap Immutability Feature Migration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the ConfigMap and Secret immutability feature: the Immutable field validation, the mutation prevention logic, and the watch optimization that skips immutable objects.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

70-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all the Go source files implementing the ConfigMap and Secret immutability feature in kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32.0. Here's a summary of what was found:

## Key Findings

**Three main layers of implementation:**

1. **API & Validation Layer** - Prevents mutations on immutable objects:
   - `ValidateConfigMapUpdate` and `ValidateSecretUpdate` functions enforce that data cannot change when `Immutable=true`
   - `ValidateImmutableField` utility validates the immutable constraint

2. **Mutation Prevention Logic** - Prevents both flag and data mutations:
   - When an object has `Immutable=true`, any attempt to modify the data fields or the immutable flag itself is rejected
   - Implemented in `pkg/apis/core/validation/validation.go` lines 6845-6851 (Secrets) and 6902-6911 (ConfigMaps)

3. **Watch Optimization** - Kubelet optimization for immutable objects:
   - `pkg/kubelet/util/manager/watch_based_manager.go` implements `objectCache.Get()` which detects immutable objects and stops their reflectors
   - `pkg/kubelet/secret/secret_manager.go` and `pkg/kubelet/configmap/configmap_manager.go` initialize the managers with immutability detection callbacks
   - When an object is marked as immutable, the kubelet stops watching for changes via `item.setImmutable()` and `item.stop()`

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol names, and a detailed narrative explaining the entire implementation.

referencedFrom types.UID) {\n254: \tkey := objectKey{namespace: namespace, name: name}\n255: \n256: \t// AddReference is called from RegisterPod thus it needs to be efficient.\n257: \t// Thus, it is only increasing refCount and in case of first registration\n258: \t// of a given object it starts corresponding reflector.\n259: \t// It's responsibility of the first Get operation to wait until referencedFrom types.UID) {\n272: \tkey := objectKey{namespace: namespace, name: name}\n273: \n274: \tc.lock.Lock()\n275: \tdefer c.lock.Unlock()\n276: \tif item, ok := c.items[key]; ok {\n277: \t\titem.refMap[referencedFrom]--\n278: \t\tif item.refMap[referencedFrom] == 0 {\n279: \t\t\tdelete(item.refMap, referencedFrom)\n280: \t\t}\n281: \t\tif len(item.refMap) == 0 {\n282: \t\t\t// Stop the underlying reflector.\n283: \t\t\titem.stop()\n284: \t\t\tdelete(c.items, key)\n285: \t\t}\n286: \t}\n287: }\n288: \n289: // key returns key of an object with a given name and namespace.\n290: // \t}\n295: \treturn name\n296: }\n297: \n298: func (c *objectCache) isStopped() bool {\n299: \tc.lock.RLock()\n300: \tdefer c.lock.RUnlock()\n301: \treturn c.stopped\n302: }\n303: \n304: func (c *objectCache) Get(namespace, name string) (runtime.Object, error) {\n305: \tkey := objectKey{namespace: namespace, name: name}\n306: \n307: \tc.lock.RLock()\n308: \titem, exists := c.items[key]\n309: \tc.lock.RUnlock()\n310: \n311: \tif !exists {\n312: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"object %q/%q not registered\", namespace, name)\n313: \t}\n314: \t// Record last access time independently if it succeeded or not.\n315: \t// This protects from premature (racy) reflector closure.\n316: \titem.setLastAccessTime(c.clock.Now())\n317: \n318: \t// Don't restart reflector if Kubelet is already shutting down.\n319: \tif !c.isStopped() {\n320: \t\titem.restartReflectorIfNeeded()\n321: \t}\n322: \tif err := wait.PollImmediate(10*time.Millisecond, time.Second, item.hasSynced); err != nil nil {\n327: \t\treturn nil, err\n328: \t}\n329: \tif !exists {\n330: \t\treturn nil, apierrors.NewNotFound(c.groupResource, name)\n331: \t}\n332: \tif object, ok := obj.(runtime.Object); ok {\n333: \t\t// If the returned object is immutable, stop the reflector.\n334: \t\t//\n335: \t\t// NOTE: we may potentially not even start the reflector if the object is\n336: \t\t// already immutable. However, given that:\n337: \t\t// - we want to also handle the case when object is marked as immutable later\n338: \t\t// - Secrets and ConfigMaps are periodically fetched by volumemanager anyway\n339: \t\t// - doing that wouldn't provide visible scalability/performance gain - we\n340: \t\t//   already have it from here\n341: \t\t// - doing that would require significant refactoring to reflector\n342: \t\t// we limit ourselves to just quickly stop the reflector here.\n343: \t\tif c.isImmutable(object) {\n344: \t\t\titem.setImmutable()\n345: \t\t\tif item.stop() {\n346: \t\t\t\tklog.V(4).InfoS(\"Stopped watching for changes - object is immutable\", \"obj\", klog.KRef(namespace, name))\n347: \t\t\t}\n348: \t\t}\n349: \t\treturn object, nil\n350: \t}\n351: \treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected object type: %v\", obj)\n352: }\n353: \n354: func (c *objectCache) startRecycleIdleWatch() {\n355: \tc.lock.Lock()\n356: \tdefer c.lock.Unlock()\n357: \n358: \tfor key, item := range c.items {\n359: \t\tif item.stopIfIdle(c.clock.Now(), c.maxIdleTime) {\n360: \t\t\tklog.V(4).InfoS(\"Not acquired for long time, Stopped watching for changes\", \"objectKey\", key, \"maxIdleTime\", c.maxIdleTime)\n361: \t\t}\n362: \t}\n363: }\n364: \n365: func (c *objectCache) shutdownWhenStopped(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n366: \t<-stopCh\n367: \n368: \tc.lock.Lock()\n369: \tdefer c.lock.Unlock()\n370: \n371: \tc.stopped = true\n372: \tfor _, item := range c.items {\n373: \t\titem.stop()\n374: \t}\n375: }\n376: \n377: // NewWatchBasedManager creates a manager that keeps a cache of all objects\n378: // necessary for registered pods.\n379: // It implements the following logic:\n380: //   - through a coordinated chain: When a pod references an immutable Secret or ConfigMap, the watch-based manager (initialized via `NewWatchingSecretManager` or `NewWatchingConfigMapManager`) starts a reflector to monitor the object.
